Users with DEFAULT Profile

USER.DEFAULTPROFILE CIS
User accounts using the DEFAULT profile
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 33 users using the DEFAULT profile.
Details 
Following limits are defined by the DEFAULT profile:

PASSWORD LIMITS:
PASSWORD_VERIFY_FUNCTION: NULL
INACTIVE_ACCOUNT_TIME: 365
PASSWORD_REUSE_TIME: UNLIMITED
PASSWORD_REUSE_MAX: UNLIMITED
PASSWORD_LOCK_TIME: 1
FAILED_LOGIN_ATTEMPTS: 10
PASSWORD_ROLLOVER_TIME: 0
PASSWORD_LIFE_TIME: 180
PASSWORD_GRACE_TIME: 7

RESOURCE LIMITS:
CPU_PER_CALL: UNLIMITED
COMPOSITE_LIMIT: UNLIMITED
SESSIONS_PER_USER: UNLIMITED
LOGICAL_READS_PER_SESSION: UNLIMITED
CONNECT_TIME: UNLIMITED
IDLE_TIME: UNLIMITED
PRIVATE_SGA: UNLIMITED
CPU_PER_SESSION: UNLIMITED
LOGICAL_READS_PER_CALL: UNLIMITED
Remarks The CIS benchmark recommends against assigning users to the DEFAULT profile as the DEFAULT profile has UNLIMITED settings for all resources, allowing the user to launch a denial-of-service attack by exhausting all resources.

The Oracle best practice is to update the DEFAULT profile to match organizational standards and use custom profiles to accommodate accounts that are an exception to the normal organizational standard.

New database users are assigned the DEFAULT profile unless another profile is explicitly assigned.

Even though profiles can be used to limit resource consumption, such as CPU and memory, Oracle Database Resource Manager is recommended for its flexible means of managing and tracking resource use.
References CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 4.4

Users with Default Passwords

USER.DEFPASSWORD STIG OBP CIS
User accounts should not have default passwords
Status Pass
Summary No unlocked user accounts are using a default password.
Remarks Default passwords for predefined Oracle accounts are well known and provide a trivial means of entry for attackers. Database or account administrators should also change well-known passwords for locked accounts. Having default passwords can lead to unauthorized data manipulation and theft of confidential information.

Note that if a script creates the database and the SYS or SYSTEM user password remains unchanged, these users are considered to possess a default password. Your database may be at risk due to the password presence within the script. Change the password to improve security.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 4.1
DISA STIG: V-237698

Users with Expired Passwords

USER.EXPIRED OBP
User accounts should not be inactive
Status Pass
Summary No unlocked users found with password expired for more than 30 days.
Remarks Password expiration is used to ensure that users change their passwords regularly. Unlocked accounts with an expired password can present a security risk, especially as those accounts age. Although the password is expired, if the account is unlocked it can easily be used by anyone knowing the old password. You should investigate accounts that have been unused for an extended period to determine whether they should remain active.
References Oracle Best Practice

Inactive Users

USER.INACTIVE STIG OBP CIS
Infrequently used accounts should be locked or dropped
Status Pass
Summary All user accounts will eventually lock when inactive. No unlocked users inactive for more than 35 days found.
Remarks If a user account is no longer in use, it unnecessarily increases the system's attack surface while providing no corresponding benefit. Furthermore, unauthorized use is less likely to be noticed when no one uses the account regularly. Investigate accounts not used for more than 35 days to determine whether they should remain active. A solution is to set INACTIVE_ACCOUNT_TIME in the profiles assigned to users to automatically lock accounts that have not logged in to the database instance for a specified number of days, for example, 35 days. Audit infrequently-used accounts for unauthorized activities.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 3.9
DISA STIG: V-237725

Sample Schemas

USER.SAMPLE STIG OBP CIS
Sample schemas should be dropped
Status Low Risk
Summary Found 2 sample schemas.
Details 
Sample schemas: HR, SH
Remarks Sample schemas are well-known accounts provided by Oracle to serve as simple examples for developers. They generally serve no purpose in a production database and should be removed because they unnecessarily increase the attack surface of the database.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 4.2
DISA STIG: V-220284

Application Owner Account

USER.APPOWNER STIG OBP
Evaluate authorizations to object owner account
Status Evaluate
Summary No application owner found.
Remarks Restricting access to application service/owner accounts is crucial, especially since these accounts typically hold sensitive data or highly privileged procedures and functions that can access and modify sensitive data. As a best practice, these accounts should be locked or converted into schema-only accounts. This prevents unauthorized users from accessing these accounts. You should audit these accounts' activity if, for any reason, they require interactive use. This finding lists the non-Oracle-maintained schema with the most number of objects.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219851

Shared Accounts

USER.SHARED STIG OBP
User accounts should not be shared
Status Pass
Summary No user is found to share administrative privileges. No Proxy user found that shares another account.
Remarks Having shared accounts to interact with the database may prevent the application from recording an individual user's identity used to read, insert, update and delete records. Use accounts assigned to individual users where feasible. You should audit shared or proxy users' activity. Configure user accounts, the database and/or the application to provide personal accountability. To accurately identify individual application users in connection pools, utilize the SET_IDENTIFIER procedure of DBMS_SESSION in SQL or the appropriate method/attribute in your programming language. Enterprise-packaged applications may have methods for achieving this, so check with the vendor and My Oracle Support for more information. It is also vital to monitor proxy users, who can connect to the database as their client users.

Also, you should not have accounts with multiple administrative privileges (sysdba, sysoper, sysbackup, sysdg, syskm). You should assign one administrative privilege per user account for better separation of duties. Users requiring to execute multiple administrative functions can have specific accounts for each activity type.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-220310, V-220311, V-220313, V-237724

Users with Objects

USER.OBJOWNER STIG
Users who own objects
Status Pass
Summary Non-Oracle maintained users that own objects not found.
Remarks Object owners can control access to their objects through Discretionary Access Control (DAC). This is the default functionality in the Oracle Database. In general, no additional action is required. If desired, Database Vault can be utilized to enable or disable a user's DAC privileges on their objects.
References DISA STIG: V-237703

Users Authorized for Object Ownership

USER.OBJAUTHZ STIG
User accounts should be authorized to own objects
Status Pass
Summary No users own database objects.
Remarks By default, users have complete control over the objects they own and can grant access to others. It is important to ensure that only documented and authorized users are allowed to own objects. Uncontrolled object ownership can result in unauthorized access, alterations, and modifications to data. Regularly review the account list for unauthorized ownership and reassign authorized objects to the appropriate authorized owner if needed.
References DISA STIG: V-220283

Users with Security Objects

USER.SECURITYOBJS STIG
Isolate program units that provide security functionality
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 2 users who own security-related objects. Found 1 schema who own Program Units and can potentially call security-related functions.
Found 2 users who can access or modify security-related objects.
Details 
Users who own security-related objects: DVF, DVSYS
Schemas containing Program Units that can potentially invoke security-
    related calls: HR
Users who can access or modify security-related objects: GSMUSER, SYSBACKUP
Remarks Stored procedures, functions, and packages that enforce or define security policies should be isolated from application code and data. An attacker can use system privileges (such as CREATE ANY TABLE, DROP ANY TABLE, ALTER ANY TABLE, INSERT ANY TABLE, DELETE ANY TABLE, UPDATE ANY TABLE, CREATE ANY PROCEDURE, DROP ANY PROCEDURE, ALTER ANY PROCEDURE, and EXECUTE ANY PROCEDURE) to manipulate security objects or data in the database. Please review PL/SQL code in functions, procedures, and packages that support security functions to determine in what schemas they are located and take appropriate action to isolate them in a separate schema. Ensure access to data through PL/SQL code that supports security functions does not exceed permitted authorization.

Oracle Label Security can tag program units as trusted and prevent unauthorized access to user data when executed by a malicious user.
References DISA STIG: V-220298

Users with Grant Option

USER.GRANTOPTION STIG OBP
Limit propagation of access rights
Status Pass
Summary No users found who have been granted privileges to perform security critical actions with grant option.
Remarks Account permission to grant privileges within the database is an administrative function. Minimizing the number and privileges of administrative accounts reduces the chances of privileged account exploitation. User accounts that require WITH GRANT OPTION privileges should belong to sanctioned users who can propagate access rights to important objects. Limiting the propagation of access rights ensures that users can't continuously grant access to objects they don't own without restriction.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219829, V-237715

Users with Sensitive Data

USER.SENSITIVEDATA STIG OBP
Check access granted on data marked sensitive by TSDP
Status Evaluate
Summary No user schema found that contains sensitive data as marked by TSDP.
Remarks In the current context, sensitive data refers to any data flagged as sensitive by Transparent Sensitive Data Protection (TSDP). To ensure secure access to sensitive information, it is best to grant access through roles rather than directly to individual accounts. Prompt revocation of access granted to individual accounts is recommended.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-237704

User Schemas in SYSTEM or SYSAUX Tablespace

USER.TABLESPACE STIG OBP
User accounts should not use SYSTEM or SYSAUX tablespaces
Status Pass
Summary No user data is stored in SYSTEM and SYSAUX tablespace by default.
Remarks The SYSTEM and SYSAUX tablespaces are reserved for Oracle-supplied user accounts. Regular user schemas should refrain from using these tablespaces to avoid a possible denial of service caused by exhausting these resources.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219847, V-219848

Legacy Password Versions

USER.AUTHLEGACY OBP
User accounts should not have legacy password versions
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 4 user accounts that require removal of older password versions. No user accounts have HTTP verifiers.
Details 
Database supports password versions up to 12C.
Users authenticated using the legacy password versions: (none)
Users with latest 12C password version and legacy password versions: HR(11G
    12C), PDBADMIN(11G 12C), SH(11G 12C), SYSTEM(11G 12C)

Users with HTTP verifiers: (none)
Remarks The database may store multiple password versions for each user account, where each version supports a different version of the password hashing algorithm. Every user account should include a version for the latest password version supported by the database so that the user can be authenticated using the latest algorithm supported by the client. When all clients have been updated, the security of user accounts can be improved by removing obsolete versions.

HTTP password verifiers are used for XML Database authentication. Use the ALTER USER command to remove these verifiers from user accounts that do not require this access.

Common users cannot be altered in a PDB.

References Oracle Best Practice

Account Locking after Failed Login Attempts

USER.NOLOCK STIG OBP CIS
Lock the account after limited number of failed login attempts
Status Pass
Summary User accounts are configured to prevent brute force password attacks by locking the account after a number of failed login attempts. User accounts are configured to stay locked for a minimum duration after being locked due to failed login attempts.
Details 
FAILED_LOGIN_ATTEMPTS:
Profiles with limited failed login attempts: DEFAULT (10), ORA_CIS_PROFILE
    (5), ORA_STIG_PROFILE (3)
Profiles with unlimited failed login attempts: (none)
Users with unlimited failed login attempts: (none)

PASSWORD_LOCK_TIME:
Profiles with minimum lock time: DEFAULT (1 day), ORA_CIS_PROFILE (1 day)
Profiles without minimum lock time: ORA_STIG_PROFILE
Users without minimum lock time: (none)
Remarks Setting FAILED_LOGIN_ATTEMPTS and PASSWORD_LOCK_TIME in user profiles is recommended to defend against password-guessing attacks. This will lock the account after a certain number of failed login attempts for a certain time. To expedite the identification and prompt response, assign temporary users to a profile tailored to their type of activity.
References Oracle Best Practice

Users with Unlimited Session Idle Time

USER.IDLETIME STIG OBP
User sessions should not be idle indefinitely
Status Low Risk
Summary Found 1 user that can remain connected to the database indefinitely without having their sessions terminated due to inactivity.
Details 
IDLE_TIME:
Profiles with limited IDLE_TIME: ORA_STIG_PROFILE (15)
Profiles with unlimited IDLE_TIME: DEFAULT, ORA_CIS_PROFILE
Users with unlimited IDLE_TIME: PDBADMIN
Remarks Sessions left open while users are absent can lead to unauthorized sensitive data access without having attackers worry about subverting privileges or breaking passwords to get access. Controlling the session's idle time is more relevant to client-server applications or terminal connections. The IDLE_TIME parameter in user profiles specifies the permitted duration of continuous inactive time during a session, after which the session is terminated.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-237738

Users with Gradual Password Rollover

USER.PASSWORDROLLOVER OBP
Disallow using both old and new passwords indefinitely when in password rollover
Status Pass
Summary No profiles found with PASSWORD_ROLLOVER_TIME set to a value greater than 0.
Remarks Gradual Password Rollover allows administrators to change application database passwords without having to schedule downtime. Before the gradual password rollover feature, the database administrator needed to take the application down while the database password was being rotated. This was because the password update required changes on both the database and the application side. With gradual database password rollover, the application can continue to use the older password until the new password is configured in the application. To accomplish this, the database administrator can associate a profile having a non-zero limit for the PASSWORD_ROLLOVER_TIME password profile parameter with an application schema. This allows the database password of the application user to be altered while allowing the older password to remain valid for the time specified by the PASSWORD_ROLLOVER_TIME limit. Try to limit the use of this feature to application schemas that need to undergo password maintenance and keep the rollover period to a minimum.
References Oracle Best Practice

Temporary Users

USER.TEMP STIG OBP CIS
Temporary accounts should be locked or dropped
Status Evaluate
Summary No users found with unlimited INACTIVE_ACCOUNT_TIME or unlimited PASSWORD_LIFE_TIME.
Remarks User accounts that are not accessed for a while and stay OPEN may not be needed on a regular basis and may have been created for temporary activities. Users designated as temporary or emergency accounts shall automatically be locked after an organization-defined period. Giving these users a tailored temporary profile that sets limits for this particular type of account helps reduce the risk of account misuse. You should review locked accounts periodically to assess if you can drop them.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 3.3, 3.9
DISA STIG: V-237741

Development Users in Production Databases

USER.DEV STIG OBP
Disallow developer user accounts in production databases
Status Evaluate
Summary It is recommended to restrict developers from modifying the production database structure or altering production data.
Remarks The database must be protected from unauthorized access by developers, and developer-type accounts should not exist in production systems unless expressly authorized. These users should not be able to create and maintain tables or other database objects. If necessary, provide developers with specific tablespaces and don't grant quota on tablespaces owning production objects. Database Vault can help establish trusted paths between applications and the database to help prevent developers from connecting from non-sanctioned servers/clients to the database.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-237706

Minimum Client Authentication Version

USER.AUTHVERSION STIG OBP
Update clients using old password versions
Status Advisory
Summary Minimum client version is not configured correctly.
Details 
SQLNET.ALLOWED_LOGON_VERSION_SERVER is not set (default value = 12).
    Recommended value is 12a.
SQLNET.ALLOWED_LOGON_VERSION_CLIENT is not set (default value = 11).
    Recommended value is 12a.
Remarks Over time, Oracle releases have added support for increasingly secure versions of the algorithm used for password authentication of user accounts. For backward client compatibility, the database keeps supporting previous password versions. The sqlnet.ora parameter ALLOWED_LOGON_VERSION_SERVER determines the minimum password version that the database will accept. Set this parameter to the highest value supported by the database for maximum security once all client systems have been upgraded. Consider evaluating before setting ALLOWED_LOGON_VERSION_SERVER to 12a as it may prevent older clients from connecting to the database instance.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219875

Privileges and Roles

Verified that no grants have been made to PUBLIC.
No user granted write on dictionary tables containing password verifiers.

Remarks Users with READ, SELECT, and UPDATE privileges on dictionary tables containing verifiers can access and modify user password verifiers. The verifiers can be used in offline attacks to discover user passwords.

Users with Administrative SYS* Privileges

PRIV.SYSADMIN STIG OBP
Segregate administrative privileges among different user accounts
Status Advisory
Summary Found 2 users granted administrative SYS* privileges. Found 3 administrative SYS* privileges not granted to any user.
Details 
SYSDBA    (2): SYS, SYSTEM
SYSOPER   (1): SYS
SYSBACKUP (0): (none)
SYSDG     (0): (none)
SYSKM     (0): (none)
Remarks Administrative SYS* privileges allow a user to perform maintenance operations, including some that may occur while the database is not open. The SYSDBA privilege allows the user to run as SYS and perform virtually all privileged operations. Starting with Oracle Database 12.1, Oracle introduced less powerful administrative privileges to allow users to perform specific administrative tasks with less than full SYSDBA privileges. To benefit from this separation of duty, you should grant each of these administrative privileges to at least one named user account.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-237709

Users with DBA Role

PRIV.DBA STIG OBP CIS
Ensure DBA and PDB_DBA roles are granted only to necessary users
Status Evaluate
Summary 2 out of 33 users have been directly or indirectly granted DBA/PDB_DBA role via 2 grants.
1 user is granted DBA/PDB_DBA role with admin option via 1 grant.
No Objects owned by DBA(s) can be accessed by non-DBA(s).
Details 
Users with highly sensitive DBA/PDB_DBA role:

PDBADMIN: PDB_DBA(*)

SYSTEM: DBA

(*) = granted with admin option
Remarks The DBA and PDB_DBA roles are powerful and can bypass many security controls. You should only grant them to a small number of trusted administrators. As a best practice, it is recommended to create custom DBA-like roles with the minimum set of privileges that users require to execute their tasks (least privilege principle) and not grant the DBA or PDB_DBA roles. Privilege Analysis can assist in identifying used/unused privileges and roles. Different roles with minimum required privileges based on the types of operations database administrators execute also help achieve Separation of Duties.

Furthermore, each trusted user should have an individual account for accountability reasons. You should audit users with the DBA or PDB_DBA roles to detect unauthorized privileged activity. Avoid granting the DBA, PDB_DBA, or custom DBA-like powerful roles with WITH ADMIN option unless necessary. Please note that Oracle may add or remove roles and privileges from the DBA or PDB_DBA role.

Commonly granted DBA role cannot be revoked in a PDB.

References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.3.3
DISA STIG: V-237710

Users with Powerful Roles

PRIV.BIGROLES STIG OBP CIS
User accounts with catalog roles should be limited
Status Evaluate
Summary 7 out of 33 users have been directly or indirectly granted powerful roles via 37 grants.
1 user is granted powerful roles with admin option via 1 grant.
Details 
Grants of AQ_ADMINISTRATOR_ROLE, EM_EXPRESS_ALL, EXP_FULL_DATABASE,
    IMP_FULL_DATABASE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE, EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE,
    DELETE_CATALOG_ROLE, OEM_MONITOR, DBA, AUDIT_ADMIN roles:

DBSNMP: OEM_MONITOR
DBSNMP <- OEM_MONITOR: SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

    EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

    IMP_FULL_DATABASE

    EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE
GSMADMIN_INTERNAL <- DATAPUMP_IMP_FULL_DATABASE <- IMP_FULL_DATABASE:
    EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

GSMCATUSER <- GSMCATUSER_ROLE: AQ_ADMINISTRATOR_ROLE
GSMCATUSER <- GSMCATUSER_ROLE <- GSMADMIN_ROLE: AQ_ADMINISTRATOR_ROLE

GSMUSER <- GSMUSER_ROLE <- DATAPUMP_EXP_FULL_DATABASE:
    EXP_FULL_DATABASE

    EXP_FULL_DATABASE: EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

    IMP_FULL_DATABASE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

SYSTEM <- DBA <- DATAPUMP_EXP_FULL_DATABASE <- EXP_FULL_DATABASE:
    EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE
SYSTEM <- DBA <- DATAPUMP_IMP_FULL_DATABASE: EXP_FULL_DATABASE,
    IMP_FULL_DATABASE

    EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

    EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE
SYSTEM <- DBA <- EXP_FULL_DATABASE: EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE,
    SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE
SYSTEM <- DBA <- IMP_FULL_DATABASE: EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE,
    SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE

(*) = granted with admin option
Remarks DBA and other similarly powerful roles (AQ_ADMINISTRATOR_ROLE, EM_EXPRESS_ALL, EXP_FULL_DATABASE, IMP_FULL_DATABASE, SELECT_CATALOG_ROLE, EXECUTE_CATALOG_ROLE, DELETE_CATALOG_ROLE, OEM_MONITOR, DBA, AUDIT_ADMIN) contain powerful privileges that attackers can use to bypass security controls. They should be granted only to a small number of trusted administrators. You should revoke the grant of these roles with the WITH ADMIN OPTION from unauthorized grantees. Auditing users with these roles is recommended to detect any unauthorized activity. Use Privilege Analysis to identify if the users used these privileges. If not, consider revoking.

Commonly granted above powerful roles cannot be revoked in a PDB.

References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.3.1, 5.3.2, 5.3.4

(C) = granted commonly
Remarks System privileges provide the ability to access data or perform administrative operations for the entire database, and users granted system privileges are generally used to perform administrative work. Consistent with the principle of least privilege, you should grant these privileges sparingly. Privilege Analysis may help determine the minimum set of privileges required by a user or a role. In some cases, it may be possible to substitute a more limited object privilege grant instead of a system privilege (ANY) grant that applies to all objects.

Avoid granting system privileges with ADMIN OPTION. You should review users with system privileges to determine if they are used to perform administrative and general user responsibilities. You should provide users with administrative and general user responsibilities with separate accounts for each duty.

Commonly granted system privileges cannot be revoked in a PDB.

References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.2.2, 5.2.10

Encryption Packages Granted to PUBLIC

PRIV.ENCRYPTPACKAGEPUBLIC CIS
Control EXECUTE grants on encryption packages to PUBLIC
Status Evaluate
Summary The EXECUTE privilege on 1 encryption package is granted to PUBLIC.
Details 
EXECUTE privilege to PUBLIC granted on: DBMS_RANDOM
Remarks Privileges granted to PUBLIC are available to all users. EXECUTE privilege on encryption-related packages allows, among other things, encrypting and decrypting stored data. If a database user needs to execute an encryption-related package, explicitly grant the privilege to the user instead of granting it to PUBLIC.

EXECUTE privilege grant on DBMS_CRYPTO and DBMS_RANDOM packages to PUBLIC should be reviewed, per your organizational security requirements. If you encrypt your data using DBMS_CRYPTO, ensure that you securely manage the encryption keys, including its lifecycle and confidentiality.

DBMS_RANDOM generates a predictable set of random values and should not be used for cryptographic purposes.
References CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.1.3

Scheduler Job Packages Granted to PUBLIC

PRIV.JOBSCHPACKAGEPUBLIC OBP CIS
Control EXECUTE grants on job scheduler packages to PUBLIC
Status Evaluate
Summary The EXECUTE privilege on 2 Job Scheduler packages is granted to PUBLIC. Found 5 users with system privilege to create a job without explicit EXECUTE on job packages but uses EXECUTE granted to PUBLIC.
Details 
EXECUTE privilege to PUBLIC granted on: DBMS_SCHEDULER, DBMS_JOB
Found 5 Users who can create jobs without explicit EXECUTE privileges on
    job packages: DBSNMP, XDB, CTXSYS, GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, SYSTEM(*)
1 user can create external scheduler jobs without explicit EXECUTE
    privilege: SYSTEM(*)
3 users who can create scheduler jobs within other schemas without explicit
    EXECUTE privilege: CTXSYS, GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, SYSTEM(*)
5 users who can create scheduler jobs whenever they want without explicit
    EXECUTE privilege: AUDSYS, DBSNMP, MDSYS, SYSTEM(*), XDB
3 users who can create scheduler jobs whenever they want without explicit
    EXECUTE privilege: CTXSYS, GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, SYSTEM(*)

(*) = granted with admin option
Remarks Privileges granted to PUBLIC are available to all users. EXECUTE privileges on Job Scheduler packages to PUBLIC allows users with system privileges (CREATE EXTERNAL JOB, CREATE ANY JOB, CREATE JOB, MANAGE SCHEDULER) to run database or operating system jobs without explicit EXECUTE privileges to run these packages. Review users with these system privileges and grant them the appropriate ones.

Please consider that a user with CREATE EXTERNAL JOB system privilege can run operating system commands outside of the database context; users with CREATE ANY JOB can run database jobs as other users and impersonate them; users with CREATE JOB can execute scripts (or SQL commands) whenever they want.

While you can REVOKE from PUBLIC and explicitly grant EXECUTE privilege on these packages (DBMS_SCHEDULER, DBMS_JOB) to specific users who need access, it's unnecessary as users will still need to have a system privilege (CREATE EXTERNAL JOB, CREATE ANY JOB, CREATE JOB, MANAGE SCHEDULER) grant to be able to execute jobs.

Oracle strongly recommends that you switch from DBMS_JOB to DBMS_SCHEDULER scheduled jobs.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.1.5

(*) = granted with admin option
Remarks Privileges granted to PUBLIC are available to all users. Credentials are database objects that hold a username/password pair for authenticating and impersonating EXTPROC callout functions, remote jobs, external jobs, and file watchers from the SCHEDULER. EXECUTE privilege on DBMS_CREDENTIAL package to PUBLIC allows users with system privileges (CREATE CREDENTIAL, CREATE ANY CREDENTIAL) to manage credentials. Review users with these system privileges and grant them the appropriate ones. While you can REVOKE from PUBLIC and explicitly grant EXECUTE privilege on DBMS_CREDENTIAL to specific users who need access, it's unnecessary as users will still need to have a system privilege (CREATE CREDENTIAL or CREATE ANY CREDENTIAL) grant to be able to manage credentials.

    execute UTL_FILE: SYSTEM, GSMUSER, GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, SYSBACKUP
Remarks Privileges granted to PUBLIC are available to all users. Granting EXECUTE privilege on file system packages to PUBLIC could allow users with system privileges (ADVISOR, CREATE ANY DIRECTORY, READ ANY DIRECTORY) or object privileges (READ or WRITE) to modify operating system files without having explicit EXECUTE privileges to run these packages. Review users with these different system and object privileges and grant them the appropriate ones.

While you can REVOKE from PUBLIC and explicitly grant EXECUTE privilege on these packages (DBMS_ADVISOR, DBMS_LOB, UTL_FILE) to specific users who need access, it's unnecessary as users will still need to have a system privilege (ADVISOR, CREATE ANY DIRECTORY, READ ANY DIRECTORY) or an object privilege (READ or WRITE) on DIRECTORY to be able to modify operating system files. Also, DBMS_LOB can be used to manipulate LOBs that are in the database. Please review the users who are authorized to execute DBMS_LOB.
References CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.1.2

Network Packages Granted to PUBLIC

PRIV.NETPACKAGEPUBLIC CIS
Control EXECUTE grants on network packages to PUBLIC
Status Evaluate
Summary The EXECUTE privilege on 5 network packages is granted to PUBLIC. Found 1 user granted network privilege via network ACLs without explicit EXECUTE on network packages but uses EXECUTE granted to PUBLIC.
Details 
EXECUTE privilege to PUBLIC granted on: DBMS_LDAP, UTL_HTTP, UTL_INADDR,
    UTL_SMTP, UTL_TCP
1 user granted network privileges via network ACLs who can use EXECUTE on
    network packages granted to PUBLIC: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL
Remarks Privileges granted to PUBLIC are available to all users. Network packages provide PL/SQL APIs to interact with or access remote servers. Granting EXECUTE privilege on network packages to PUBLIC does not allow an unauthorized user or attacker to connect to a remote server and exfiltrate data. If a database user needs to move data through the network packages, the user will need to be authorized via an ACL using DBMS_NETWORK_ACL_ADMIN and DBMS_NETWORK_ACL_UTILITY packages.

DBMS_LDAP requires authentication prior to using other functions.

Oracle best practice is to control the use of packages and to NOT revoke the grants from PUBLIC.
References CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.1.1

JAVA Packages Granted to PUBLIC

PRIV.JAVAPACKAGEPUBLIC CIS
Control EXECUTE grants on Java packages to PUBLIC
Status Evaluate
Summary The EXECUTE privilege on 1 Java package is granted to PUBLIC. Found 1 user is granted JAVA_ADMIN to administer Java permissions without direct EXECUTE on Java packages but uses EXECUTE privilege granted to PUBLIC.
Details 
EXECUTE privilege to PUBLIC granted on: DBMS_JAVA
1 user is granted JAVA_ADMIN role and can administer Java policies without
    direct EXECUTE privilege on Java packages: SYSTEM
Remarks EXECUTE privilege on Java packages (DBMS_JAVA, DBMS_JAVA_TEST) could allow an attacker to run operating system commands from the database. Only JAVA_ADMIN users can grant permission to other users to access various Java classes. EXECUTE privilege to PUBLIC allows users to administer Java policies without explicit privileges to run these packages.

You should review EXECUTE privilege on Java packages granted to PUBLIC per your organizational standard to prevent an unauthorized user from using Java function. Additionally, the JAVA_ADMIN role should be granted only to authorized users.
References CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.1.4

SQL Packages Granted to PUBLIC

PRIV.QUERYPACKAGEPUBLIC CIS
Control EXECUTE grants on packages that allows SQL as input to PUBLIC
Status Evaluate
Summary The EXECUTE privilege on 5 packages that take SQL query as input is granted to PUBLIC.
Details 
EXECUTE privilege to PUBLIC granted on: DBMS_XMLQUERY, DBMS_XMLSAVE,
    DBMS_XMLSTORE, DBMS_XMLGEN, DBMS_SQL
Remarks Privileges granted to PUBLIC are available to all users. EXECUTE privilege on packages that allow SQL execution or DML operations could allow an attacker to inject malicious SQL in vulnerable PL/SQL procedures - and perform a SQL injection attack - which could lead to sensitive data exposure.

While you can REVOKE from PUBLIC and explicitly grant EXECUTE privilege on these invokers' rights packages (DBMS_SQL, DBMS_REDACT, DBMS_XMLGEN, DBMS_XMLQUERY, DBMS_XMLSAVE, DBMS_XMLSTORE) to specific users who need access, it is more effective to review PL/SQL code and ensure the use of bind variables instead of concatenating SQL statements with strings. When SQL statements employ string concatenation, they become vulnerable to potential SQL injection attacks through malicious inputs.
References CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.1.6

Users with direct object privileges on tables that hold sensitive data should also be reviewed. In addition to minimizing grants of these privileges, consider using Database Vault realms to limit the use of these privileges to access sensitive data stored in user schemas. Privilege Analysis may help you identify the underlying objects being accessed via the broad privilege and help you substitute it with a more limited object privilege grant. You should avoid granting broad data access system privileges with ADMIN option, as the recipient will be able to grant the privilege further.

    DELETE on SYS.INCEXP, DELETE on SYS.INCFIL, DELETE on SYS.INCVID,
    INSERT on SYS.INCEXP, INSERT on SYS.INCFIL, INSERT on SYS.INCVID,
    UPDATE on SYS.INCEXP, UPDATE on SYS.INCFIL, UPDATE on SYS.INCVID

    DELETE on SYS.INCEXP, DELETE on SYS.INCFIL, DELETE on SYS.INCVID,

    SYS.EXPIMP_TTS_CT$

WMSYS: DELETE on SYS.NOEXP$, INSERT on SYS.NOEXP$
Remarks Users with these privileges can directly modify objects in the SYS, DVSYS, AUDSYS, or LBACSYS schemas. Manipulating these system objects may allow security protections to be circumvented or otherwise interfere with the normal operation of the database. You should not grant access to objects in SYS, DVSYS, AUDSYS, and LBACSYS schemas to PUBLIC. When running a Privilege Analysis Capture, be aware of privileges granted to access objects in any Oracle-created schemas. Review those privilege grants for relevance.

Commonly granted write privileges on SYS, DVSYS, AUDSYS or LBACSYS objects cannot be revoked in a PDB.

References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 5.1.3.1, 5.1.3.2, 5.1.3.3
DISA STIG: V-220266, V-237708

Users Who Can Impersonate Other Users

PRIV.IMPERSONATEUSER OBP CIS

Authorization Control

Database Vault

AUTHZ.DATABASEVAULT STIG OBP GDPR
Ensure separation of duties and limit sensitive data access
Status Advisory
Summary Database Vault is not enabled.
Remarks Database Vault offers customizable policies to regulate the actions of privileged database accounts, such as those used by administrative users, applications, and utilities. Internal and external threats can exploit privileged account credentials to access sensitive information. Database Vault realms protect sensitive data from unauthorized access, even by users with system privileges. Command rules in Database Vault limit accidental or malicious execution of SQL commands. You can enforce separation of duties to prevent a single all-powerful user and use trusted paths to restrict further access to sensitive data based on system factors such as IP address, program name, time of day, and user name. Database Vault Operations Control can be used to restrict common users from accessing data local to pluggable databases (PDB). Database Vault Operations Control can be used to restrict common users from accessing pluggable database (PDB) local data in autonomous, regular Cloud or on-premises environments.
References Oracle Best Practice
EU GDPR: Article 6, 25, 29, 32, 34, 89; Recital 28, 29, 78, 156
DISA STIG: V-220266

Privilege Analysis

AUTHZ.PRIVANALYSIS OBP
Implement the principle of least privilege
Status Advisory
Summary Privilege Analysis policies not found. Privilege Analysis has never been run.
Details 
Users who can start the privilege analysis capture process: SYSTEM
Remarks Privilege Analysis dynamically analyzes privilege and role usage in real time, providing insight into actual use by database users and application service accounts. This feature helps strengthen security by identifying unused or redundant privileges and roles, allowing administrators to determine the minimum privileges required for users or applications to function correctly. Administrators can confidently revoke unnecessary privileges with clear visibility into assigned privileges and their usage. Privilege Analysis helps implement the least privilege model and minimize the risk of intentional or accidental abuse of privileges.
References Oracle Best Practice

Authentication for Client Scripts

AUTHZ.PASSWORDSCRIPTS STIG OBP
Check user account passwords within scripts and batch jobs
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 5 password-authenticated users whose passwords can potentially be embedded in client scripts, jobs, and application source code to connect to the database server.
Details 
Users with a password that can be embedded in client scripts: HR, PDBADMIN,
    SH, SYS, SYSTEM
Remarks Typically, users (including applications, batch jobs, and scripts) connect to databases using a standard CONNECT statement specifying a database connection string. This string often includes the username and password in clear text. Embedding credentials (hardcoded credentials) into source code is highly discouraged. It poses significant security risks and makes it harder to comply with password expiration and rotation mandates. A better alternative is to use Oracle Key Vault (OKV) or a Secure External Password Store (SEPS), so application users, batch jobs, and scripts can connect to the database without having the password written in the code. With OKV, an authorized client can fetch a database user password in real time and connect to the database without storing the password. With SEPS, the database credentials, username, and password are securely stored in an Oracle Keystore created for this purpose. It is essential to thoroughly review client code to detect the presence of passwords in clear text. Additionally, applications should employ measures to conceal any authentication information displayed following a successful or unsuccessful connection attempt.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-220303, V-220304, V-237734

Data Masking

AUTHZ.DATAMASKING STIG OBP GDPR
Anonymize sensitive data in non-production environments
Status Evaluate
Summary No table is marked as containing sensitive data. Found 3 users who can transfer sensitive data.
Details 
Users that can transfer sensitive data: SYSTEM, GSMUSER, GSMADMIN_INTERNAL
Remarks Clones of live production data are typically shared with development, testing, and data analytics teams so that they have access to realistic data to support their activities. Attackers have learned that valuable and sensitive data often ends up in non-production environments, which are generally less protected than production. Masking sensitive data before handing it over to development and analytics teams eliminates the risk of data breaches in non-production environments by irreversibly replacing the original sensitive data with realistic but fictitious data. Procedures that ensure copies of production data are kept away from non-secured locations must also be in place. Oracle Data Safe or Oracle Data Masking and Subsetting Pack can help you anonymize sensitive data transferred to non-production systems.
References Oracle Best Practice
EU GDPR: Article 5; Recital 26
DISA STIG: V-219844, V-220299

Fine-Grained Access Control

Data Redaction

ACCESS.DATAREDACTION GDPR
Redact sensitive data for read-only application screens
Status Advisory
Summary No data redaction policies found.
Details 
Users exempted from Data Redaction Policies: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, GSMUSER,
    SYSTEM
Users who can create or manage Data Redaction Policies: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL,
    GSMUSER, SYSTEM
Remarks Data Redaction automatically masks sensitive data found in the results of a database query. The data is dynamically masked before it is returned as part of the result set, so it does not interfere with any conditions specified as part of the query. Data Redaction is mainly used to redact data in read-only scenarios (e.g., read-only screens, REST GET APIs). The redaction policy will not affect access by users with the EXEMPT REDACTION POLICY privilege. Users who can execute the DBMS_REDACT package can create and modify redaction policies. Also, consider using Oracle Data Safe or Oracle Data Masking and Subsetting Pack to permanently mask sensitive data when making copies for test or development.
References EU GDPR: Article 6, 25, 32, 34, 89; Recital 28, 29, 78, 156

Virtual Private Database

ACCESS.VPD GDPR
Control access to sensitive data at the row level
Status Advisory
Summary No VPD policies found that automatically limit access to certain rows and/or columns based upon the user or the database environment.
Details 
Users exempted from VPD Policies: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, GSMUSER
Users who can create or manage VPD Policies: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, GSMUSER,
    MDSYS, SYSTEM, WMSYS, XDB
Remarks Virtual Private Database (VPD) allows for fine-grained control over which rows and columns of a table are visible to a SQL statement. Access control using VPD limits each database session to only the specific data it should be able to access. Access by users with the EXEMPT ACCESS POLICY privilege will not be affected by VPD policies. Users who can execute the DBMS_RLS package can create and modify these policies. Evaluate Real Application Security before implementing VPD, especially for new custom applications.
References EU GDPR: Article 29, 32

Real Application Security

ACCESS.RAS GDPR
Control access to sensitive data at the row and column level
Status Advisory
Summary No RAS policies found.
Details 
Users not impacted by RAS Policies: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, GSMUSER
Users who can create or manage RAS policies: DBSFWUSER, SYSTEM, SYSTEM
Remarks Real Application Security (RAS) is a more modern, advanced version of Virtual Private Database. It provides fine-grained control over the rows and columns of a table that are visible to a SQL statement. RAS data access policies use a declarative syntax based on access control lists. Access by users with the EXEMPT ACCESS POLICY privilege will not be affected by RAS access policies. Users with ADMIN_SEC_POLICY and APPLY_SEC_POLICY privileges can create and modify these policies.
References EU GDPR: Article 6, 25, 32, 34, 89; Recital 28, 29, 64, 78, 156

Label Security

ACCESS.LABELSECURITY GDPR
Classify sensitive data and authorize access using labels
Status Advisory
Summary Label Security is not enabled.
Remarks Oracle Label Security (OLS) provides a framework for implementing and enforcing multi-level security (MLS) policies within a database. MLS is a security model that allows you to classify data into different security levels and assign users different levels of clearance for accessing that data. With OLS, you can define classification labels, associate them with table rows, and then control access to the rows based on the security labels and the user's clearance level. This helps to ensure that sensitive information is protected and only available to authorized users. Access by users with the EXEMPT ACCESS POLICY privilege will not be affected by the Label Security policies. Each policy has a corresponding administrative role; users who have this role can administer the policy.

Starting Oracle Database 23ai, Oracle Label Security cannot be used with Oracle Internet Directory (OID) since Directory Integration Platform is being deprecated. Oracle recommends moving from OLS-OID configuration to stand-alone OLS configuration before upgrading to Oracle Database 23ai.
References EU GDPR: Article 18, 29, 32; Recital 67

Transparent Sensitive Data Protection (TSDP)

ACCESS.TSDP OBP
Classify and transparently protect sensitive data
Status Advisory
Summary No data tagged with sensitive types found.
Details 
Policies: (none)
Users with EXECUTE on SYS.DBMS_TSDP_MANAGE: (none)
Users with EXECUTE on SYS.DBMS_TSDP_PROTECT: (none)
Remarks Transparent Sensitive Data Protection (TSDP) allows a sensitive type (such as a Credit Card number) to be associated with each column that contains sensitive data. TSDP policy can apply data security controls such as Data Redaction, auditing, VPD, and even mask bind values (in auditing and trace files) to all instances of that particular type so that protection is uniform and consistent. Users who can execute the DBMS_TSDP_MANAGE and DBMS_TSDP_PROTECT packages can manage sensitive data types and the security controls applied by the TSDP policies.
References Oracle Best Practice

Unified Audit Trail: In use, 13809 records found (Oct 18 2024 - Dec 14
    2024)
Remarks Auditing plays a crucial role in overseeing the operations of any system, including those performed by highly privileged users. With the introduction of Unified Auditing in Oracle Database 12c, auditing has become more streamlined and secure. This feature consolidates all database sources of audit logs into a single, easily manageable trail and adds powerful conditional auditing capabilities. While the AUDIT_SYSLOG_LEVEL parameter helps send condensed audit records to a remote syslog collector, a more secure and comprehensive approach would be to use Oracle Data Safe or Oracle Audit Vault and Database Firewall. These tools streamline the implementation of a widely recognized best practice and common regulatory requirement, which mandates the transfer of audit data from databases to a separate server while maintaining full audit record details.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.2.2
EU GDPR: Article 30, 33, 34
DISA STIG: V-219862, V-220267, V-220270, V-220271, V-220272, V-220273, V-220274, V-220275, V-237747

Remarks The Unified Auditing feature in Oracle Database allows you to capture all audit activity in a single, central location. It also introduces a new syntax for creating more detailed and specific audit policies, enabling you to build conditions and add exclusions. In addition, the database provides a set of pre-defined audit policies that you can use to meet frequent audit requirements. Review enabled and disabled audit policies to ensure you are meeting your auditing requirements. However, care must be taken while configuring audit policies for ALL actions and for ALL users to prevent generation of huge volume of audit trails.
References Oracle Best Practice
EU GDPR: Article 30, 33, 34
DISA STIG: V-237747

Fine Grained Audit

AUDIT.FGA STIG OBP
Check need for column level auditing using FGA
Status Advisory
Summary No fine grained audit policies found.
Details 
No object found with fine grained auditing enabled.
Users with EXECUTE on SYS.DBMS_FGA: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, GSMUSER, SYSTEM
Remarks Fine-Grained Audit (FGA) policies can audit data access based on content. Using FGA policies, you can specify the columns and conditions for which you want to generate audit records. This effectively audits targeted data access while avoiding unnecessary audit records that correspond to regular activity. FGA policies also allow an event handler to be specified. This event handler is a PL/SQL function that, for example, can warn a database administrator of suspicious activity. You should only use FGA policies if a unified audit policy cannot answer the requirements.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-220276

Audit Administrative (SYS*) Users

AUDIT.ADMINACTIONS STIG OBP CIS
Ensure Administrative users' actions are audited
Status Evaluate
Summary Actions of all the admin users are audited.
Details 
Unified Audit policies enabled for administrators:
ALL USERS (ORA$DICTIONARY_SENS_COL_ACCESS, ORA_DV_DEFAULT_PROTECTION,
    ORA_DV_SCHEMA_CHANGES, ORA_LOGIN_LOGOUT, ORA_SECURECONFIG)
Remarks It is crucial to audit administrative actions performed by the SYS user. Remember that traditional audit policies do not apply to SYS, and in that case, the AUDIT_SYS_OPERATIONS parameter must be set to record SYS actions to a separate audit trail. With Unified Audit policies, you can monitor the actions of the SYS user and those of other users. Make sure that all your SYS* users' activities are audited.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.2.1
DISA STIG: V-219868

Audit User Logon and Logoff

AUDIT.CONNECTIONS OBP CIS
Check auditing for logins and logouts
Status Pass
Summary Database connection events are audited for all users.
Details 
Unified audit - auditing enabled: LOGOFF, LOGON
Users audited using unified auditing: ALL USERS
Unified audit - Policies Used: ORA_DV_SCHEMA_CHANGES
Remarks As a best practice, you should audit successful and unsuccessful connections to the database. Connection auditing is valuable information for forensic analysis. Unsuccessful connection attempts can provide early warning of an attacker's attempt to access the database. Auditing the LOGOFF time helps understand how long the session was active. You should enable auditing for LOGON and LOGOFF actions for all the required users.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 6.1.18, 6.2.27

Audit Conditions

AUDIT.CONDITION OBP
Use audit conditions to reduce the number of audit records
Status Evaluate
Summary No unified audit policies are using conditions.
Remarks Unified Audit enables the specification of a condition that determines whether auditing is performed for an action. If the WHEN clause condition evaluates to TRUE, then auditing occurs; else, it does not. Some security-relevant use cases of conditional auditing include auditing user activity for direct database access (bequeath), activity during non-business hours, access to sensitive data through untrusted paths, and in the absence of a specific parameter value on a SYS_CONTEXT namespace.
References Oracle Best Practice

Audit Shared Accounts

AUDIT.SHAREDPROXY STIG OBP
Audit shared or proxy user's activity
Status Evaluate
Summary No shared users found.
Remarks Having shared accounts to interact with the database may prevent the application from recording an individual user's identity used to insert/update/read/delete records. Use accounts assigned to individual users where feasible. You should audit shared or proxy users' activity. Configure user accounts, the database and/or the application to provide personal accountability. Activity performed under a shared account must include the end user in the audit log.

Also, you should not have accounts with multiple administrative privileges. You should assign each administrative privilege to one user account for better separation of duties. Uses requiring to execute multiple administrative functions can have specific accounts for each activity type.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-220313

Audit Storage

AUDIT.TABLESPACE STIG OBP
Audit trail should be stored on a tablespace of its own
Status Advisory
Summary One or more audit trail is in SYSAUX tablespace. Examined 3 audit trails. Audit tablespace with acceptable free space.
Details 
STANDARD AUDIT TRAIL is in SYSAUX
UNIFIED AUDIT TRAIL is in SYSAUX
FGA AUDIT TRAIL is in SYSAUX
13809 Records found in Unified Audit Trail from Oct 18 2024 to Dec 14 2024
No audit cleanup job configured to clean audit trails.
Remarks Auditing is the most effective way to record what happens in the database. Auditing tracks the use of privileges, activities of highly privileged users, access to sensitive data, actions performed on database objects, and modifications made to database settings. Auditing can be helpful for forensic investigations in the event of a data breach and to demonstrate regulatory compliance. Database audit trails use the SYSAUX tablespace by default and can fill it up. That can affect other database operations that rely on that tablespace. If the tablespace exhausts, audit record writes will spill over to OS audit files, and a message is written to the ALERT LOG. If the OS file system space also becomes full, audited operations will start to fail.

It is recommended to relocate the audit trail to another tablespace using DBMS_AUDIT_MGMT.SET_AUDIT_TRAIL_LOCATION procedure. Relocating to a dedicated tablespace will improve system performance and eliminate the probability of some other component taking up the free space. You can encrypt the new tablespace. Also, make sure you allocate adequate space. Oracle recommends that you configure a different tablespace for the audit trail. You can encrypt the new tablespace. Also, make sure you allocate adequate space.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-220305, V-237717, V-237718

Encryption

Transparent Data Encryption

ENCRYPT.TDE STIG OBP GDPR
Ensure tablespace encryption is used to secure data-at-rest
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 5 unencrypted tablespaces. No encrypted columns found.
Details 
Unencrypted tablespaces: SYSAUX, SYSTEM, TEMP, UNDOTBS1, USERS
Encrypted tablespaces: (none)

TABLESPACE_ENCRYPTION = MANUAL_ENABLE for databases running on-premises.
Remarks Encryption of sensitive data is a requirement in most regulated environments. Transparent Data Encryption (TDE) automatically encrypts data as it is stored and decrypts it upon retrieval. TDE protects sensitive data from attacks that bypass the database and read data files directly. Encryption keys may be stored in wallets on the database server itself or stored remotely in Oracle Key Vault for improved security. Additionally, attackers often leverage non-encrypted sensitive data for extortion or threaten to release sensitive data publicly (ransomware). Encryption keys may be stored in wallets on the database server itself or stored remotely in Oracle Key Vault for improved security. The parameter TABLESPACE_ENCRYPTION supersedes (replaces) ENCRYPT_NEW_TABLESPACES and ensures that TDE tablespace encryption is applied to all newly created tablespaces. Setting TABLESPACE_ENCRYPTION parameter to AUTO_ENABLE or ENCRYPT_NEW_TABLESPACES parameter to ALWAYS is recommended in order to protect all data regardless of the options specified when the tablespace is created.

Starting with Oracle Database 23ai, the encryption algorithms 'SEED 128 bits key' and 'GOST 256 bits key' have been de-supported.

With the exception of the HP Itanium platform, the GOST and SEED decryption libraries are deprecated with Oracle Database 23ai. Oracle recommends that you (online or offline) re-key TDE encrypted data with another algorithm at the earliest.
References Oracle Best Practice
EU GDPR: Article 6, 32, 34; Recital 83
DISA STIG: V-220297, V-237740

Encryption Key Wallet

ENCRYPT.WALLET STIG OBP GDPR
Check the location of your encryption wallet
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 1 wallet. No wallets are stored in the data file directory.
Details 
WALLET_ROOT init.ora parameter is not set.
Wallet type: FILE
Status: NOT_AVAILABLE
Wallet was created using mkstore utility.
Wallet order: SINGLE

Data file directory: /opt/oracle/product/23ai/dbhomeFree/dbs
Remarks Wallets are encrypted files that store encryption keys, passwords, and other sensitive data. You should not store wallet files in the same directory with database data files to avoid accidentally creating backups that include both encrypted data files and the wallet containing the master key protecting those files. Consider storing encryption keys in Oracle Key Vault instead of wallet files for maximum separation of keys and data.
References Oracle Best Practice
EU GDPR: Article 6, 32, 34; Recital 83
DISA STIG: V-220290

FIPS Mode for TDE and DBMS_CRYPTO

ENCRYPT.DBFIPS STIG
Use FIPS 140-2 approved cryptographic modules for STIG compliance
Status Evaluate
Summary FIPS mode is disabled for Transparent Data Encryption (TDE) and DBMS_CRYPTO PL/SQL package.
Details 
DBFIPS_140 = FALSE.
Remarks Federal Information Processing Standard (140-2) is a U.S. government security standard that specifies security requirements for cryptographic processing. It is used to approve cryptographic modules. Setting parameter DBFIPS_140 to TRUE enables Transparent Data Encryption (TDE) and DBMS_CRYPTO PL/SQL package program units to run in a FIPS-compliant mode. FIPS mode is mainly used by departments and agencies of the United States federal government looking to meet FIPS and/or STIG compliance.
References DISA STIG: V-237739, V-237740

FIPS mode for TLS

ENCRYPT.TLSFIPS STIG
Database network traffic should be protected through TLS
Status Evaluate
Summary FIPS 140-2 authentication/encryption is not configured.
Details 
SSLFIPS_140 is not set (default value = FALSE).
Remarks Federal Information Processing Standard (140-2) is a U.S. government security standard that specifies security requirements. It is used to approve cryptographic modules. Setting parameter SSLFIPS_140 = TRUE makes Transport Layer Security (TLS) cryptographic operations take place in the underlying FIPS-certified library. The CPU accelerates these cryptographic operations when hardware acceleration is available and configured correctly in the host hardware and software. FIPS mode is mostly used by departments and agencies of the United States federal government looking to meet FIPS and/or STIG compliance.
References DISA STIG: V-220294

Authentication Configuration

CONF.AUTHN OBP CIS
Check number of failed authentication attempts in a session
Status Pass
Summary Examined 2 initialization parameters. No issues found.
Details 
SEC_MAX_FAILED_LOGIN_ATTEMPTS = 3
RESOURCE_LIMIT = TRUE
Remarks SEC_MAX_FAILED_LOGIN_ATTEMPTS configures the maximum number of failed authentication attempts in a single session before the connection is closed.

This is independent of the user profile parameter FAILED_LOGIN_ATTEMPTS, which controls locking the user account after multiple failed login attempts. Not controlling failed login attempts before closing the connection and locking accounts after a number of failed logins opens the door for successful brute-force login and Denial-of-Service attacks. RESOURCE_LIMIT should be set to TRUE to enable enforcement of any resource constraints defined in user profiles.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.2.10, 2.2.16

PDB OS User

CONF.DEFAULTPDBOSUSER OBP CIS
Ensure the highly privileged Oracle OS user is not being used to run external OS jobs from the database
Status Medium Risk
Summary Oracle OS user will be used to interact with the operating system.
Details 
Operating system interactions are performed as the Oracle OS user.
Remarks The PDB_OS_CREDENTIAL parameter determines the OS user for running external jobs from within the Oracle Database at operating system (OS) level. This parameter is set to a credential defined using the DBMS_CREDENTIAL package.

Allowing a job to execute at OS level using the default credential, Oracle OS user, or other OS administrative users may grant excessive privileges beyond necessary. Using a least privileged OS user defined by a specified credential value in the PDB_OS_CREDENTIAL parameter helps ensure that operating system interactions are performed with minimal privileges, providing more secure operating system interactions. You should create an OS user with minimum necessary privileges and use it to set the PDB_OS_CREDENTIAL parameter.

This approach helps protect data belonging to one PDB from being accessed by users connected to another PDB. A less privileged OS user also prevents unauthorized activities.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.2.17

Control Files

CONF.CONTROLFILES STIG OBP
Ensure control files have redundancy
Status Medium Risk
Summary Found 2 control files.
Details 
Control file(s) location: /opt/oracle/oradata/FREE/control01.ctl,
    /opt/oracle/oradata/FREE/control02.ctl

All control files are in same directory.
Remarks A control file tracks the physical components of the database. It is the root file that the database uses to find all the other files used by the database. Loss of access to the control files can affect database availability, integrity, and recovery. Due to the importance of the control file and to reduce the risk of losing it due to corruption, or accidental or intentional removal, Oracle recommends that the control file be multiplexed or have multiple identical copies. Organizations using RAID policies for multiplexing must review them to ensure control files are on separate, archived directories within one or more RAID devices.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219827

Redo Log Files

CONF.REDOLOGS STIG OBP
Ensure redo log files have redundancy
Status Evaluate
Summary Found 3 redo log files.
Details 
Redo files: /opt/oracle/oradata/FREE/redo01.log,
    /opt/oracle/oradata/FREE/redo02.log,
    /opt/oracle/oradata/FREE/redo03.log
Remarks The redo log is the most crucial structure for recovery operations, which consists of two or more pre-allocated files that store all changes made to the database as they occur. Every instance of an Oracle Database has an associated redo log to protect the database in case of an instance failure. Redo logs should be multiplexed and stored on different physical disks.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219828

Archive Log Mode

CONF.ARCHIVELOG STIG OBP
Archive log mode should be enabled
Status Evaluate
Summary Database in NOARCHIVELOG mode.
Remarks In NOARCHIVELOG mode, a clean shutdown and database shutdown are necessary to create a backup. If a failure occurs, restoring the whole database to the latest backup is the only recovery option. This mode may result in the loss of recent transactions. On the other hand, ARCHIVELOG mode allows backups during operation, ensuring the ability to recover the database to a specific point in time in the event of failure or data corruption.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219849, V-220296

Database Backup

CONF.BACKUP STIG OBP
Ensure regular database backup
Status Evaluate
Summary No Backup Records found for the last 90 days.
Remarks You should backup the database regularly. Having a recent backup on a separate media will help you prevent data loss in a system failure and may help you quickly recover from a ransomware attack. Oracle Recovery Manager (RMAN) allows performing backup and recovery tasks on your databases.

It is strongly recommended to use Transparent Data Encryption (TDE) or RMAN encrypted backups to ensure that malicious users cannot read backup data. Encrypting data at the source with TDE or RMAN protects local and subsequent offsite backups from the beginning of the backup lifecycle.

For continuous data protection and fast recovery against ransomware attacks, refer to Oracle Zero Data Loss Recovery Appliance, which provides immutable backups and deployment in network-isolated Cyber Vault architecture.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-237720, V-237721, V-237722

SQL Firewall

CONF.SQLFIREWALL OBP
Check SQL Firewall configuration
Status Advisory
Summary SQL Firewall is not enabled.
Remarks Built into Oracle Database kernel, SQL Firewall inspects all the incoming SQL statements and database connections and can detect and/or block unauthorized SQL and connections. SQL Firewall provides real time protection against common database attacks such as SQL Injection. Once activated, SQL Firewall will learn SQL and connection activities and build user based allow-lists from collected data; the allow-lists can be modified and enforced in a desired mode.

Network Communication

CONF.NETWORK OBP CIS
Check remote listener and protocol error parameters
Status Pass
Summary Examined 4 initialization parameters that can be used to detect malformed packets from a client and found no issue.
Details 
REMOTE_LISTENER = (none)
SEC_PROTOCOL_ERROR_FURTHER_ACTION = (DROP,3)
SEC_PROTOCOL_ERROR_TRACE_ACTION = TRACE
SEC_RETURN_SERVER_RELEASE_BANNER = FALSE
Remarks The REMOTE_LISTENER parameter is used to connect a client application to a database instance that is located on a different machine than the listener. In typical single-instance deployments, only a local listener is used, and this parameter should be unset. However, in high availability configurations such as Oracle Real Application Clusters (RAC) environments, the REMOTE_LISTENER parameter should be set. Please check RAC best practices to ensure all database instances can register with all the listener processes. This establishes client connections even if one listener process or database instance fails.

The SEC_PROTOCOL_ERROR parameters control the database server's response to malformed network packets from a client. The SEC_PROTOCOL_ERROR_FURTHER_ACTION parameter is set to DROP by default, and SEC_PROTOCOL_ERROR_TRACE_ACTION is set to TRACE. A malicious client attempting to attack the database may send malformed packets. To log the incident and terminate the connection, you should set these parameters appropriately.

Setting SEC_RETURN_SERVER_RELEASE_BANNER to FALSE is essential to limit the amount of information disclosed to an unauthenticated client. This parameter ensures that only minimal information is provided to the client, enhancing security by reducing the amount of information potential attackers can use.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.2.5, 2.2.11, 2.2.12, 2.2.13

Database Links

CONF.DATABASELINKS STIG OBP CIS
Check Database Links
Status Evaluate
Summary No database links found. Database link names may differ from the remote database connection they define.
Details 
GLOBAL_NAMES = FALSE

Users with CREATE DATABASE LINK privilege: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL(*),
    GSMUSER(*), SYSTEM
Users with CREATE PUBLIC DATABASE LINK privilege: GSMADMIN_INTERNAL, SYSTEM
Remarks Database links allow users to execute SQL statements referencing tables in other databases. This allows both querying and storing data on the remote database.

Public database links are visible to all users, while private database links are only visible to the link owner.

Avoid using public database links as much as possible, as all users who connect to the database will have access to them. This can create a potential security vulnerability if the appropriate access controls are not in place.

It is advisable to set GLOBAL_NAMES to TRUE to ensure that link names match the databases they access.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.2.3, 4.6

Network Configuration

Network Encryption

NET.ENCRYPTION STIG OBP CIS
Check configurations used for Native Network Encryption
Status Advisory
Summary Native network encryption is accepted but not required. Integrity check using checksums is accepted but not required.
Details 
SQLNET.ENCRYPTION_SERVER is not set (default value = ACCEPTED).
SQLNET.CRYPTO_CHECKSUM_SERVER is not set (default value = ACCEPTED).


No valid listeners found.

SSL_CERT_REVOCATION is not set (default value = NONE).
Remarks Network encryption is crucial for protecting the confidentiality and integrity of communication between a database server and its clients. To ensure that client connections are encrypted, you should configure either Native Encryption or TLS.

If using Native Encryption, it's essential to set both ENCRYPTION_SERVER and CRYPTO_CHECKSUM_SERVER to REQUIRED. Oracle Database servers and clients are configured to ACCEPT encrypted connections by default to make deployment and compatibility easier. This means you can enable encryption and integrity settings for a connection pair by configuring just one side of the connection (server-side or the client-side). For instance, if many Oracle clients connect to a database instance, you can configure the required encryption and integrity settings for all those connections by modifying the sqlnet.ora file on the server end. There's no need to make configuration changes for each client separately. However, remember that the risk of plaintext data passing over the network still exists.

Note that whether the security service is enabled depends on a combination of client and server configuration parameters.

If using TLS, it's crucial to specify TCPS for all network ports, and SSL_CERT_REVOCATION should be set to REQUIRED. Oracle recommends using TLS network encryption.
References Oracle Best Practice
CIS Benchmark: Recommendation 2.3.1, 2.3.2
DISA STIG: V-219841, V-220263, V-220291, V-237699, V-237700, V-237723

    is YES.

Remarks TCP.VALIDNODE_CHECKING should be enabled to control which client nodes can connect to the database server. You can specify an allow list containing client nodes (IP Address/Hostname/Subnet) that are allowed to connect (TCP.INVITED_NODES) or a blocklist of nodes that are not allowed (TCP.EXCLUDED_NODES). You should not configure both the invited and excluded nodes list. If that is the case, the database will use only the invited node list.

Check parameters that control connections waiting for authentication

Remarks Unauthenticated connections can introduce possible denial-of-service attacks, wherein malicious clients attempt to flood database servers with connect requests that consume resources. OS.MULTIDB STIG
Check presence of production and non-production databases on the same host
Status Pass
Summary Only one database/instance configured on the host
Details 
Database/instance on the host: (none)
Remarks Production and non-production databases must be segregated and not coexist in the same host. If a host contains both a development and a production database, determine if developers were granted elevated database and/or operating system privileges as they can affect the production database system's operation and/or security. Operating system and database privileges assigned to developers on shared development and production systems must be restricted. Details 
Owner: oracle
Command: /opt/oracle/product/23ai/dbhomeFree/bin/tnslsnr LISTENER -inherit
Remarks Listener processes accept incoming network connections and connect them to the appropriate database server process. These processes should run with a user ID separate from the database and agent processes. You should administer these processes only through local OS authentication.
References DISA STIG: V-219838

CMAN Remote Admin

OS.CMANLOCAL STIG OBP
Check local Connection Manager
Status Pass
Summary Oracle Connection Manager not found on this host.
Remarks Oracle Connection Manager is a proxy server that forwards connection requests to databases or other proxy servers. As remote administration provides a potential opportunity for malicious users to make unauthorized changes to the Connection Manager configuration or interrupt its service, it should not be used. As a best practice, Oracle CMAN should be installed on a computer separate from the database server and client computers.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219874

Diagnostic Destination

OS.DIAGNOSTICDEST STIG OBP
Check file permissions for directories holding diagnostic data
Status Medium Risk
Summary Diagnostic destination configured. The diagnostic directory permission is not configured correctly.
Details 
Diagnostic destination: /opt/oracle/diag.

Permission error:
/opt/oracle/diag has permission (rwxrwxr-x) should be (rwxr-x---)
Remarks The DIAGNOSTIC_DEST initialization parameter specifies where the trace, alert, core, and incident directories and files are located. These files may contain sensitive data or information that could prove helpful to potential attackers. Access to the diagnostics directory should only be granted to the Oracle process and software owner accounts, Administrators, DBAs, System group, or developers authorized to debug the database application. Document and authorize user access requests to the directory outside the Oracle, DBA, and system administrators' account list.
References Oracle Best Practice
DISA STIG: V-219873

OS.FILEPERMISSIONS STIG OBP

Executables in $ORACLE_HOME/bin: 208 (0 permission errors)
Configuration files in $TNS_ADMIN: 2 (0 permission errors)
Data files in $ORACLE_HOME/dbs: 5 (0 permission errors)
Libraries in $ORACLE_HOME/lib: 216 (0 permission errors)
Remarks The ORACLE_HOME directory and its subdirectories contain files critical to the correct operation of the database, including executable programs, libraries, data files, and configuration files. Operating system file permissions must not allow users other than the ORACLE_HOME owner to modify these files. They must not allow other users to read the contents of Oracle data files directly.
References Oracle Best Practice

This report provides information and recommendations that may be helpful in securing your Oracle database system. These recommendations reflect best practices for database security and should be part of any strategy for Data Protection by Design and by Default. These practices may help in addressing Articles 25 and 32 of the EU General Data Protection Regulation as well as other data privacy regulations. Technical controls alone are not sufficient for compliance. Passing all findings does not guarantee compliance.

Apart from Oracle Best Practices, findings in this report map to DISA Oracle Database 12c STIG V2R8 Group IDs, CIS Benchmark for Oracle Database 19c v1.2.0 recommendations, and EU GDPR 2016/679 articles and recitals.

Oracle Database Vault, Oracle Advanced Security, Oracle Label Security, Oracle Data Masking and Subsetting Pack are database licensed options. Oracle Key Vault and Oracle Audit Vault and Database Firewall require separate licensing as well.
